## ğŸ“Š Types of Technical Interviews

### Know What You're Facing ğŸ¯

```bash
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
# INTERVIEW TYPES & FORMATS
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   CODING INTERVIEWS                        â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

ğŸ“Š Frequency: 90% of tech companies
â±ï¸ Duration: 45-60 minutes
ğŸ¯ Focus: Data structures & algorithms

What to Expect:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
1. Introduction (5 min)
   â€¢ Interviewer introduces themselves
   â€¢ You introduce yourself
   â€¢ Brief background

2. Problem Statement (5 min)
   â€¢ Interviewer gives problem
   â€¢ Ask clarifying questions
   â€¢ Understand requirements
   â€¢ Discuss edge cases

3. Solution Development (30-40 min)
   â€¢ Think out loud
   â€¢ Start with brute force
   â€¢ Optimize
   â€¢ Code solution
   â€¢ Test with examples

4. Follow-up Questions (5-10 min)
   â€¢ Optimization discussions
   â€¢ Alternative approaches
   â€¢ Edge cases
   â€¢ Time/space complexity

5. Your Questions (5 min)
   â€¢ Ask about team/role
   â€¢ Show interest

Common Problem Types:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Array manipulation
â€¢ String processing
â€¢ Tree/Graph traversal
â€¢ Dynamic programming
â€¢ Recursion
â€¢ Sorting/Searching
â€¢ Hash tables
â€¢ Two pointers
â€¢ Sliding window

Difficulty Distribution:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Entry Level: 70% Easy, 30% Medium
â€¢ Mid Level: 20% Easy, 70% Medium, 10% Hard
â€¢ Senior: 10% Easy, 60% Medium, 30% Hard
â€¢ Staff+: System design focus (less coding)

Platforms Used:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ CoderPad (most common)
â€¢ HackerRank (online assessments)
â€¢ CodeSignal
â€¢ Google Docs (Google)
â€¢ Whiteboard (in-person)
â€¢ IDE (take-home)

Tips:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âœ… Think out loud (very important!)
âœ… Start with brute force
âœ… Discuss before coding
âœ… Test your code
âœ… Handle edge cases
âœ… Optimize if time allows

âŒ Don't code in silence
âŒ Don't give up early
âŒ Don't argue with interviewer
âŒ Don't ignore hints

â•‘                   SYSTEM DESIGN INTERVIEWS                 â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

ğŸ“Š Frequency: Senior+ (3+ years), some mid-level
â±ï¸ Duration: 45-60 minutes
ğŸ¯ Focus: Architecture, scalability, trade-offs

What to Expect:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
1. Problem Statement (5 min)
   "Design Twitter"
   "Design URL shortener"
   "Design YouTube"

2. Requirements Gathering (10 min)
   â€¢ Functional requirements
   â€¢ Non-functional requirements
   â€¢ Scale expectations
   â€¢ Constraints

3. High-Level Design (15 min)
   â€¢ Draw architecture diagram
   â€¢ Major components
   â€¢ Data flow
   â€¢ APIs

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
1. "Tell me about yourself"

STAR Method:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Structure every answer:

S - Situation
  â€¢ Set the context
  â€¢ Brief background

T - Task
  â€¢ What needed to be done
  â€¢ Your responsibility

A - Action
  â€¢ What YOU did
  â€¢ Specific steps taken
  â€¢ Most important part!

R - Result
  â€¢ Outcome
  â€¢ What you learned
  â€¢ Quantify if possible

Example:
"Tell me about a challenging project"

S: "In my last role, we had a legacy system causing
    frequent outages."

T: "I was tasked with investigating and fixing the
    root cause while maintaining uptime."

A: "I analyzed logs, identified a memory leak,
    proposed a refactoring plan, and led a team
    of 3 developers to implement it over 2 months."

R: "We reduced outages by 90%, improved response
    time by 40%, and saved the company $50K/year
    in downtime costs."

  â€¢ Success story
  â€¢ Failure story
  â€¢ Conflict resolution
  â€¢ Leadership
  â€¢ Learning experience
  â€¢ Technical challenge
  â€¢ Tight deadline
  â€¢ Disagreement

â–¡ Make stories adaptable to multiple questions
â–¡ Practice out loud
â–¡ Time yourself (2-3 min per story)

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
```

```bash
â€¢ Access: O(1)
â€¢ Search: O(n)
â€¢ Insert/Delete: O(n)
â€¢ Traversal techniques
â€¢ In-place modifications
â€¢ Subarrays

â€¢ Two pointers
â€¢ Sliding window
â€¢ Kadane's algorithm
â€¢ Dutch national flag

â–¡ Best Time to Buy/Sell Stock
â–¡ Maximum Subarray
â–¡ Product of Array Except Self

â–¡ Find Minimum in Rotated Sorted Array

â€¢ ASCII vs Unicode
â€¢ Character arrays

â–¡ Valid Anagram
â–¡ Longest Substring Without Repeating
â–¡ Valid Parentheses
â–¡ Longest Palindromic Substring
â–¡ Group Anagrams
â–¡ Palindrome Permutation

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

7. Heaps (Priority Queue) â­â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Frequency: 10% of problems

Must Know:
â€¢ Min-heap vs Max-heap
â€¢ Insert/Extract: O(log n)
â€¢ Heapify: O(n)
â€¢ Top K problems

Common Patterns:
â€¢ Top K elements
â€¢ Merge K lists
â€¢ Median finding

Essential Problems:
â–¡ Kth Largest Element
â–¡ Top K Frequent Elements
â–¡ Merge K Sorted Lists
â–¡ Find Median from Data Stream
â–¡ K Closest Points to Origin

Practice: 10-12 problems

8. Tries â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Frequency: 5% of problems

Must Know:
â€¢ Prefix tree structure
â€¢ Insert/Search: O(L) where L = length
â€¢ Autocomplete
â€¢ Dictionary operations

Essential Problems:
â–¡ Implement Trie
â–¡ Word Search II
â–¡ Design Add and Search Words
â–¡ Replace Words

Practice: 5-8 problems

9. Advanced Structures â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Less common but important:

â€¢ Connected components
â€¢ Cycle detection
â€¢ Dynamic connectivity

Essential Problems:
â–¡ Number of Connected Components
â–¡ Graph Valid Tree
â–¡ Redundant Connection

Practice: 6-8 problems

Segment Trees / Fenwick Trees:
â€¢ Range queries
â€¢ Rare in interviews
â€¢ Know concepts only

â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

1. Sorting & Searching â­â­â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Binary Search:
â€¢ Must implement from scratch
â€¢ Many variations
â€¢ O(log n)
â€¢ Practice: 15 problems

Merge Sort:
â€¢ Understand concept
â€¢ O(n log n)
â€¢ Stable sort
â€¢ Divide and conquer

Quick Sort:
â€¢ Understand concept
â€¢ O(n log n) average
â€¢ In-place
â€¢ Partitioning

Built-in Sort:
â€¢ Know your language's sort
â€¢ Custom comparators
â€¢ Time complexity: O(n log n)

2. Graph Algorithms â­â­â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

DFS (Depth-First Search):
â€¢ Recursive or stack
â€¢ O(V + E)
â€¢ Path finding
â€¢ Cycle detection

BFS (Breadth-First Search):
â€¢ Queue-based
â€¢ O(V + E)
â€¢ Shortest path (unweighted)
â€¢ Level-order traversal

Dijkstra's Algorithm:
â€¢ Shortest path (weighted)
â€¢ Priority queue
â€¢ O((V + E) log V)
â€¢ For non-negative weights

Topological Sort:
â€¢ DAG ordering
â€¢ Dependency resolution
â€¢ Kahn's algorithm

3. Dynamic Programming â­â­â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Pattern:
â€¢ Break into subproblems
â€¢ Memoization or tabulation
â€¢ Optimal substructure

Types:
â€¢ 1D DP
â€¢ 2D DP
â€¢ Knapsack
â€¢ Subsequence/Substring

Essential Problems:
â–¡ Climbing Stairs
â–¡ House Robber
â–¡ Coin Change
â–¡ Longest Increasing Subsequence
â–¡ Edit Distance
â–¡ Longest Common Subsequence
â–¡ 0/1 Knapsack
â–¡ Word Break

Practice: 25-30 problems (most important!)

4. Greedy Algorithms â­â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Pattern:
â€¢ Make locally optimal choice
â€¢ Hope for global optimum
â€¢ Proof required (but not in interview)

Essential Problems:
â–¡ Jump Game
â–¡ Gas Station
â–¡ Meeting Rooms II
â–¡ Task Scheduler
â–¡ Non-overlapping Intervals

Practice: 10-12 problems

5. Backtracking â­â­â­â­
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Pattern:
â€¢ Try all possibilities
â€¢ Prune invalid paths
â€¢ Recursion + undo

Essential Problems:
â–¡ Subsets
â–¡ Permutations
â–¡ Combination Sum
â–¡ N-Queens
â–¡ Word Search
â–¡ Letter Combinations

Must Know Big-O:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

O(1) - Constant:
â€¢ Array access: a[5]
â€¢ Hash table insert/lookup (average)
â€¢ Examples: Get/set variable

O(log n) - Logarithmic:
â€¢ Binary search
â€¢ Balanced tree operations
â€¢ Examples: Find in BST

O(n) - Linear:
â€¢ Single loop
â€¢ Array traversal
â€¢ Examples: Find max in array

O(n log n) - Linearithmic:
â€¢ Efficient sorting
â€¢ Merge sort, Quick sort
â€¢ Examples: Sorting array

O(nÂ²) - Quadratic:
â€¢ Nested loops
â€¢ Bubble sort
â€¢ Examples: Check all pairs

O(2â¿) - Exponential:
â€¢ Recursive fibonacci (naive)
â€¢ Subsets generation
â€¢ Examples: All combinations

O(n!) - Factorial:
â€¢ Permutations
â€¢ Traveling salesman (brute force)
â€¢ Examples: All orderings

Common Optimizations:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Hash table: O(nÂ²) â†’ O(n)
â€¢ Sorting: O(nÂ²) â†’ O(n log n)
â€¢ Binary search: O(n) â†’ O(log n)
â€¢ DP: O(2â¿) â†’ O(nÂ²)

Interview Expectation:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
```

```bash
âŒ Wrong Approach:

â€¢ New problems you haven't seen

âœ… Right Approach:
"I'll learn 15-20 patterns and recognize them"
â€¢ ~20 patterns cover 80% of problems
â€¢ Pattern recognition is a skill
â€¢ Apply pattern to new problems
â€¢ Confidence in interviews

Pattern-Based Learning:

Step 1: Learn Pattern
â€¢ Understand the technique
â€¢ See 2-3 examples
â€¢ Understand when to use

Step 2: Practice Pattern
â€¢ Solve 8-10 problems with this pattern
â€¢ Variations of the pattern
â€¢ Build muscle memory

Step 3: Recognize Pattern
â€¢ New problem â†’ Identify pattern
â€¢ Apply technique
â€¢ Solve faster

Result: 150 problems with patterns > 500 random problems
```

### Master the Interview Process ğŸ—£ï¸

```bash
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
# CODING INTERVIEW EXECUTION
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   THE 7-STEP FRAMEWORK                     â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Use EVERY Interview - Non-Negotiable!

Step 1: Listen Carefully (2 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âœ… Don't interrupt
âœ… Take notes
âœ… Pay attention to ALL details
âœ… Note constraints
âœ… Look for hints in problem statement

Example:
Interviewer: "Given an array of integers and a target..."
You: [Writing down] "Array of integers, target value..."

Step 2: Ask Clarifying Questions (3-5 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Must Ask About:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Input:
â–¡ "What's the size of the array?"
â–¡ "Can the array be empty?"
â–¡ "Can it have duplicates?"
â–¡ "Are elements sorted?"
â–¡ "Can values be negative?"

Output:
â–¡ "Should I return indices or values?"
â–¡ "One solution or all solutions?"
â–¡ "Any specific format required?"

Edge Cases:
â–¡ "What if no solution exists?"
â–¡ "What if input is null?"
â–¡ "What about integer overflow?"

Constraints:
â–¡ "Any memory constraints?"
â–¡ "Time limit?"
â–¡ "Can I modify the input?"
â–¡ "Can I use extra space?"

Example Dialogue:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
You: "Just to clarify, the array contains integers -
      can they be negative?"
Interviewer: "Yes, both positive and negative."

You: "And are the integers sorted?"
Interviewer: "No, unsorted."

You: "Should I return the indices or the actual values?"
Interviewer: "Return the indices."

You: "Great, and if there's no solution, return?"
Interviewer: "Return an empty array."

You: "Perfect, let me work through an example..."

Step 3: Work Through Examples (3-5 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Always Do This:
âœ… Start with given example
âœ… Create your own examples
âœ… Test edge cases:
  - Empty input
  - Single element
  - All same elements
  - Maximum size
  - Negative numbers (if applicable)

Example:
"Let me trace through this example:
 Input: [2, 7, 11, 15], target = 9

 - Start at 2: Need 7 to make 9
 - Found 7 at index 1
 - Return [0, 1]

 Let me check an edge case:
 Input: [], target = 9
 - Empty array, return []"

Think Out Loud!
This is CRITICAL - interviewer needs to follow your thinking.

Step 4: Explain Your Approach (5 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Do NOT start coding yet!

Discuss:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Brute Force First:
"The naive approach would be to check all pairs...
 This would be O(nÂ²) time, O(1) space"

Ask If Acceptable:
"Should I code this up, or would you like to see
 if we can optimize?"

Optimized Approach:
"We could use a hash table to get O(n) time...
 This uses O(n) extra space, but saves time"

Trade-offs:
"The trade-off is space for time. Worth it given
 the constraint that n can be large."

Get Approval Before Coding:
"Does this approach sound good to you?"
[Wait for confirmation]

Why This Matters:
âœ… Shows you can think before coding
âœ… Gives interviewer chance to guide you
âœ… Prevents coding wrong solution for 30 minutes
âœ… Demonstrates communication

Step 5: Write Code (15-20 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

While Coding:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Talk Through Everything:
"I'm creating a hash table to store numbers we've seen...
 Using a dictionary here for O(1) lookup...
 First, let's check if array is null..."

Keep It Clean:
âœ… Proper variable names (not x, y, temp)
âœ… Consistent style
âœ… Comments for complex parts
âœ… Handle edge cases as you go

Bad Practices:
âŒ Coding in silence (NEVER do this!)
âŒ Messy, unreadable code
âŒ No edge case handling
âŒ Long functions without breaking down

Step 6: Test Your Code (5-7 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Don't Say: "Looks good to me!"
Do Say: "Let me trace through this with examples."

Test Cases:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â–¡ Normal case
  Input: [2, 7, 11, 15], target = 9
  Expected: [0, 1]

â–¡ Edge case: Empty array
  Input: [], target = 9
  Expected: []

â–¡ Edge case: No solution
  Input: [1, 2, 3], target = 10
  Expected: []

â–¡ Edge case: Duplicates
  Input: [3, 3], target = 6
  Expected: [0, 1]

How to Trace:
"Let me walk through with [2, 7, 11, 15], target = 9:
 - i=0, num=2, complement=7, not found, add 2 to map
 - i=1, num=7, complement=2, found in map! return [0,1]
 Looks correct!"

Find Your Own Bugs:
âœ… Shows thoroughness
âœ… Better than interviewer finding them
âœ… Demonstrates debugging skills

Step 7: Analyze Complexity (2-3 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Always Discuss:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Time Complexity:
"Time complexity is O(n) because we iterate once through
 the array and hash table operations are O(1)"

Space Complexity:
"Space complexity is O(n) in worst case where we store
 all elements in the hash table"

Can It Be Better?:
"Given we need to check all elements at least once,
 O(n) time is optimal. We could reduce space by sorting
 first and using two pointers, but that would take
 O(n log n) time."

Trade-offs:
"This solution trades space for time. The brute force
 O(nÂ²) time with O(1) space vs this O(n) time with O(n) space."

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   COMMUNICATION TECHNIQUES                 â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Think Out Loud - The Golden Rule:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Why It's Critical:
âœ… Interviewer sees your thought process
âœ… They can guide you if you're stuck
âœ… Shows problem-solving approach
âœ… Demonstrates communication skills
âœ… Reduces stress (conversation vs test)

What to Say:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

When Stuck:
âŒ "I don't know" [Silent]
âœ… "Let me think about this. I could try approach X,
    but I'm concerned about time complexity. Let me
    consider if there's a better way..."

When Considering Options:
âœ… "I'm thinking about two approaches. The first would be
    to use a hash table, which gives us O(n) time but
    uses extra space. The second would be to sort first,
    which would be O(n log n) time but O(1) space."

When Writing Code:
âœ… "I'm creating a variable to track the maximum...
    Now I'll iterate through the array...
    Here I'm updating if we found a better answer..."

Phrases to Use:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Starting:
â€¢ "Let me make sure I understand the problem..."
â€¢ "Can I work through an example first?"
â€¢ "Let me think about the approach..."

Proposing Solutions:
â€¢ "One way to solve this would be..."
â€¢ "The naive approach would be..."
â€¢ "We could optimize this by..."

Checking Understanding:
â€¢ "Does that make sense?"
â€¢ "Am I on the right track?"
â€¢ "Is this the approach you'd like me to code?"

When Stuck:
â€¢ "I'm considering a few options here..."
â€¢ "Let me think about this differently..."
â€¢ "Could I get a hint on how to handle X?"

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   HANDLING DIFFICULT MOMENTS               â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

When Completely Stuck:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

DON'T:
âŒ Sit in silence
âŒ Give up
âŒ Say "I don't know, moving on"
âŒ Get defensive

DO:
âœ… Verbalize your thoughts
  "I'm trying to figure out how to handle X. Let me think
   about what data structure would help here..."

âœ… Try different angles
  "The brute force would be O(nÂ²). To get to O(n), I'd need
   constant lookup time. Hash table could work for that..."

âœ… Ask for a hint (if really stuck)
  "I'm stuck on optimizing this part. Could you give me a
   hint on the right direction?"

âœ… Start with brute force
  "I know this isn't optimal, but let me code the brute force
   first and then we can optimize together"

When You Make a Mistake:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

DON'T:
âŒ Panic
âŒ Try to hide it
âŒ Argue with interviewer

DO:
âœ… Acknowledge it
  "Oh, you're right, I made an error there"

âœ… Fix it calmly
  "Let me correct that. It should be..."

âœ… Learn from it
  "Good catch, I need to handle that edge case"

When Running Out of Time:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

DON'T:
âŒ Rush and write buggy code
âŒ Give up

DO:
âœ… Prioritize
  "I have a few minutes left. Let me finish the core logic
   and mention edge cases I would handle"

âœ… Explain what you'd do
  "If I had more time, I would add error handling here
   and optimize this section"

âœ… Show you understand the full picture
  "The complete solution would also need to handle X, Y, Z"

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   CODE QUALITY CHECKLIST                   â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Before Saying "I'm Done":
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

â–¡ Code Readability
  âœ… Meaningful variable names
  âœ… Consistent formatting
  âœ… Logical structure
  âœ… No overly complex lines

â–¡ Edge Cases Handled
  âœ… Null/empty input
  âœ… Single element
  âœ… All same elements
  âœ… Boundary conditions

â–¡ Testing
  âœ… Traced through normal case
  âœ… Tested edge cases
  âœ… Found and fixed bugs

â–¡ Complexity Analysis
  âœ… Stated time complexity
  âœ… Stated space complexity
  âœ… Discussed trade-offs

â–¡ Communication
  âœ… Explained approach clearly
  âœ… Discussed alternatives
  âœ… Answered questions confidently
```

### Architecture at Scale ğŸ“

```bash
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
# SYSTEM DESIGN MASTERY
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   WHEN YOU NEED SYSTEM DESIGN              â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

By Level:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Entry-level (0-2 years): Rarely
â€¢ Mid-level (2-4 years): Sometimes
â€¢ Senior (4-7 years): Always!
â€¢ Staff+ (7+ years): Major focus

By Company:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ FAANG: Mid-level and above
â€¢ Startups (large): Senior and above
â€¢ Startups (small): Senior and above
â€¢ Enterprise: Senior and above

Preparation Time Needed:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Minimum: 2-3 weeks
â€¢ Recommended: 1-2 months
â€¢ Ideal: 2-3 months (with coding prep)

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   SYSTEM DESIGN FRAMEWORK                  â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

The RADIO Framework (45 min):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

R - Requirements (5-10 min)
A - API Design (5 min)
D - Data Model (5 min)
I - Initial Design (10-15 min)
O - Optimization & Deep Dive (15-20 min)

Step 1: Requirements (5-10 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Functional Requirements:
What should the system do?

Example: Design Twitter
â–¡ Users can post tweets (280 characters)
â–¡ Users can follow other users
â–¡ Users can see home timeline (tweets from followees)
â–¡ Users can search tweets

Non-Functional Requirements:
How should the system behave?

â–¡ High availability (99.9% uptime)
â–¡ Low latency (< 200ms for timeline)
â–¡ Eventual consistency (OK for follower counts)
â–¡ Handle 100M daily active users
â–¡ Handle 500M tweets per day

Scale Estimates:
â–¡ Write vs Read ratio (1:100 for Twitter)
â–¡ Storage needs (500M tweets Ã— 280 bytes)
â–¡ Bandwidth requirements
â–¡ Peak traffic (3x average)

Out of Scope (Clarify):
â–¡ Analytics
â–¡ Recommendations
â–¡ Ads
â–¡ DMs (direct messages)

Step 2: API Design (5 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Define Core APIs:

POST /api/tweet
Request: { user_id, content, media_urls }
Response: { tweet_id, created_at }

GET /api/timeline/{user_id}
Query params: ?page=1&limit=20
Response: { tweets: [...], next_page }

POST /api/follow
Request: { follower_id, followee_id }
Response: { success }

GET /api/search
Query params: ?q=keyword&page=1
Response: { tweets: [...] }

Step 3: Data Model (5 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Users Table:
user_id (PK)
username
email
created_at

Tweets Table:
tweet_id (PK)
user_id (FK)
content
created_at
like_count
retweet_count

Follows Table:
follower_id (FK) + followee_id (FK) = Composite PK
created_at

Step 4: Initial High-Level Design (10-15 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Draw Components:

[Client Apps] (Web, Mobile, Desktop)
      â†“
[Load Balancer]
      â†“
[API Gateway]
      â†“
[Application Servers] (Microservices)
  - Tweet Service
  - Timeline Service
  - User Service
  - Search Service
      â†“
[Cache Layer] (Redis)
      â†“
[Database] (PostgreSQL - Primary/Replica)
      â†“
[Object Storage] (S3 for media)

[Message Queue] (Kafka for async tasks)

Explain Flow:
1. User posts tweet â†’ API Gateway
2. Tweet Service validates, stores in DB
3. Async job publishes to followers' timelines (fanout)
4. Timeline cached in Redis
5. User requests timeline â†’ served from cache

Step 5: Optimization & Deep Dive (15-20 min)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Interviewer Will Ask:

"How do you handle hot users with millions of followers?"

Answer:
- Hybrid fanout: Fanout for normal users, on-demand for celebrities
- Pre-compute timelines for active users
- Rate limiting on posting

"How do you scale the database?"

Answer:
- Sharding by user_id (consistent hashing)
- Read replicas for read-heavy workload
- Separate DB for tweets vs users
- Archive old tweets to cold storage

"How do you ensure low latency?"

Answer:
- Cache aggressively (Redis for timelines, CDN for media)
- Pagination to limit data transfer
- Compress responses
- Connection pooling
- Async processing for non-critical tasks

"How do you handle failures?"

Answer:
- Multiple availability zones
- Database replication
- Circuit breakers
- Graceful degradation (show cached timeline if DB down)
- Monitoring and alerts

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   CORE CONCEPTS TO KNOW                    â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

1. Load Balancing
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Distribute traffic across servers
â€¢ Algorithms: Round-robin, Least connections, IP hash
â€¢ Health checks
â€¢ Examples: NGINX, AWS ELB

2. Caching
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Cache-aside (lazy loading)
â€¢ Write-through
â€¢ Write-behind
â€¢ Eviction policies: LRU, LFU, FIFO
â€¢ Examples: Redis, Memcached

3. Database Scaling
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Vertical Scaling:
â€¢ Bigger machine (limited ceiling)

Horizontal Scaling:
â€¢ Sharding (partition data)
â€¢ Replication (primary-replica)

Sharding Strategies:
â€¢ Range-based
â€¢ Hash-based
â€¢ Directory-based

4. CAP Theorem
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Pick 2 of 3:
â€¢ Consistency
â€¢ Availability
â€¢ Partition Tolerance

In distributed systems, partition tolerance is required.
So choose: CP (Consistent) or AP (Available)

Examples:
â€¢ CP: MongoDB, HBase
â€¢ AP: Cassandra, DynamoDB

5. Database Types
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

SQL (Relational):
â€¢ PostgreSQL, MySQL
â€¢ ACID guarantees
â€¢ Structured data
â€¢ Complex queries

NoSQL:
â€¢ Document: MongoDB (flexible schema)
â€¢ Key-Value: Redis, DynamoDB (high performance)
â€¢ Column: Cassandra (time-series data)
â€¢ Graph: Neo4j (relationships)

6. Message Queues
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Decouple services
â€¢ Async processing
â€¢ Handle traffic spikes
â€¢ Examples: Kafka, RabbitMQ, AWS SQS

7. CDN (Content Delivery Network)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Cache static content globally
â€¢ Reduce latency
â€¢ Offload traffic from origin
â€¢ Examples: CloudFlare, AWS CloudFront

8. Microservices vs Monolith
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Monolith:
âœ… Simple to develop
âœ… Easy to deploy
âŒ Hard to scale
âŒ Technology lock-in

Microservices:
âœ… Independent scaling
âœ… Technology flexibility
âœ… Fault isolation
âŒ Complex deployment
âŒ Network overhead

9. API Gateway
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Single entry point
â€¢ Authentication
â€¢ Rate limiting
â€¢ Request routing
â€¢ Examples: Kong, AWS API Gateway

10. Consistency Patterns
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Strong Consistency:
â€¢ Read always returns latest write
â€¢ Slower
â€¢ Example: Bank transactions

Eventual Consistency:
â€¢ Reads may return stale data temporarily
â€¢ Faster
â€¢ Example: Social media likes

â•‘                   COMMON SYSTEM DESIGN QUESTIONS           â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Must Prepare These:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1. Design URL Shortener (like bit.ly)
   â€¢ Simple starter question
   â€¢ Hash function, collision handling
   â€¢ Custom URLs
   â€¢ Analytics

2. Design Twitter/Instagram
   â€¢ Timeline generation (fanout)
   â€¢ Follow relationships
   â€¢ Media storage
   â€¢ Search

3. Design WhatsApp/Messenger
   â€¢ Real-time messaging (WebSockets)
   â€¢ Message delivery guarantees
   â€¢ Online status
   â€¢ Group chats

4. Design YouTube/Netflix
   â€¢ Video upload and processing
   â€¢ CDN for streaming
   â€¢ Recommendations
   â€¢ View counts

5. Design Uber/Lyft
   â€¢ Real-time location tracking
   â€¢ Matching algorithm
   â€¢ Payment processing
   â€¢ Surge pricing

   â€¢ Token bucket algorithm
   â€¢ Distributed rate limiting
   â€¢ Redis-based

   â€¢ URL frontier
   â€¢ Politeness
   â€¢ Duplicate detection
   â€¢ Distributed crawling

   â€¢ Replication
   â€¢ Conflict resolution (vector clocks)

   â€¢ Fanout on write vs read
   â€¢ Ranking algorithm
   â€¢ Pagination

    â€¢ Multiple channels (email, SMS, push)
    â€¢ Delivery guarantees
    â€¢ Rate limiting per user

â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âœ… Ask clarifying questions
âœ… Start with simple design, then iterate
âœ… Draw diagrams (very important!)
âœ… Explain trade-offs
âœ… Discuss failure scenarios
âœ… Mention monitoring and alerting
âœ… Think about scale
âœ… Consider cost

DON'T:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ Jump into details immediately
âŒ Design for infinite scale
âŒ Forget about data modeling
âŒ Ignore non-functional requirements
âŒ Stay silent while thinking
âŒ Be dogmatic about solutions

Remember:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"There's no single right answer in system design.
 Show your thought process, consider trade-offs,
 and demonstrate you can build scalable systems."
```

### Master the Soft Skills ğŸ¤

```bash
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
# BEHAVIORAL INTERVIEW SUCCESS
# â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   WHY BEHAVIORAL INTERVIEWS MATTER         â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

The Reality:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
You can ace all technical rounds...
But fail behavioral interview!

Companies Evaluate:
â€¢ Culture fit
â€¢ Communication skills
â€¢ Leadership potential
â€¢ Problem-solving approach
â€¢ Conflict resolution
â€¢ Growth mindset
â€¢ Teamwork
â€¢ Values alignment

Frequency: 100% of companies have behavioral rounds

Weight: 30-40% of final decision

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   THE STAR METHOD                          â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Structure EVERY Answer Using STAR:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

S - Situation (20%)
  â€¢ Set the context
  â€¢ Brief background
  â€¢ When and where?
  â€¢ Keep it concise (2-3 sentences)

T - Task (10%)
  â€¢ What needed to be done?
  â€¢ Your specific responsibility
  â€¢ The challenge or goal

A - Action (50%)
  â€¢ What YOU did (not "we")
  â€¢ Specific steps taken
  â€¢ Why you chose this approach
  â€¢ Most important part!
  â€¢ Spend majority of time here

R - Result (20%)
  â€¢ Outcome
  â€¢ What you learned
  â€¢ Quantify if possible
  â€¢ Impact on team/company

Example Question: "Tell me about a challenging project"
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Bad Answer (No Structure):
"I worked on a challenging project where the API was slow.
 It was really hard but we fixed it and it got faster."

âŒ Vague
âŒ No specifics
âŒ "We" instead of "I"
âŒ No measurable result

Good Answer (STAR Method):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

S: "In my last role at Company X, we had a critical API
    that was taking 3-5 seconds to respond, causing
    frequent timeouts and user complaints."

T: "I was tasked with investigating the root cause and
    reducing the response time to under 500ms within
    2 weeks, without requiring major architecture changes."

A: "I started by analyzing the API logs and database
    queries. I discovered three main issues:
    1) N+1 query problem in the ORM
    2) Missing database index on a frequently queried column
    3) No caching layer

    I proposed a three-part solution:
    1) Refactored queries to use eager loading
    2) Added composite index on the lookup columns
    3) Implemented Redis caching for frequently accessed data

    I wrote tests to ensure no regressions, deployed
    to staging first, monitored metrics, then rolled
    out to production gradually."

R: "The API response time dropped from 3-5 seconds to
    200-300ms - a 95% improvement. User complaints
    decreased by 80% in the first week. The solution
    required no infrastructure changes and cost only
    2 weeks of development time. I documented the
    approach and shared it with the team, which they
    later applied to optimize other endpoints."

âœ… Clear structure
âœ… Specific numbers
âœ… "I" not "we"
âœ… Measurable results
âœ… Shows initiative and impact

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   COMMON BEHAVIORAL QUESTIONS              â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Top 20 Questions (Prepare Stories For Each):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1. Tell me about yourself
   â€¢ Not in resume
   â€¢ 2-minute elevator pitch
   â€¢ Current role â†’ Past â†’ Why this company

2. Why do you want to work here?
   â€¢ Research company beforehand
   â€¢ Specific reasons (not just "great company")
   â€¢ Connect to your goals

3. Tell me about a challenging project
   â€¢ Technical complexity
   â€¢ Timeline pressure
   â€¢ How you overcame obstacles

4. Describe a time you failed
   â€¢ Real failure (not humble-brag)
   â€¢ What you learned
   â€¢ How you've improved
   â€¢ Don't blame others

5. Conflict with a coworker
   â€¢ How you resolved it
   â€¢ Communication approach
   â€¢ What you learned
   â€¢ Professional outcome

6. Time you showed leadership
   â€¢ Even if not official leader
   â€¢ Initiative taken
   â€¢ Impact on team
   â€¢ Results

7. Disagreement with manager/decision
   â€¢ How you handled it professionally
   â€¢ Your perspective
   â€¢ Outcome
   â€¢ Respect for authority

8. Biggest weakness
   â€¢ Real weakness
   â€¢ What you're doing to improve
   â€¢ Not: "I work too hard" ğŸ™„
   â€¢ Good: "Public speaking - taking courses"

9. Proudest achievement
   â€¢ Significant impact
   â€¢ Your specific role
   â€¢ Measurable results
   â€¢ Why it matters

10. How do you handle stress/pressure?
    â€¢ Specific example
    â€¢ Coping strategies
    â€¢ Successful outcome

11. Time you had to learn something quickly
    â€¢ Context
    â€¢ Learning approach
    â€¢ Applied it successfully

12. Mistake you made and how you handled it
    â€¢ Own the mistake
    â€¢ How you fixed it
    â€¢ Preventive measures

13. Working with difficult person
    â€¢ Professional approach
    â€¢ Communication strategies
    â€¢ Positive outcome

14. Time you missed a deadline
    â€¢ What happened
    â€¢ How you communicated
    â€¢ What you learned
    â€¢ Preventive steps

    â€¢ How you reacted
    â€¢ Changes you made
    â€¢ Growth demonstrated

    â€¢ Extra initiative
    â€¢ Impact
    â€¢ Why you did it

    â€¢ Context
    â€¢ Options considered
    â€¢ Decision rationale
    â€¢ Outcome

    â€¢ Time management
    â€¢ Prioritization approach
    â€¢ Communication with stakeholders

    â€¢ Your specific role
    â€¢ Collaboration
    â€¢ Team outcome

20. Why are you leaving your current job?
    â€¢ Positive framing
    â€¢ Growth opportunity
    â€¢ Never badmouth current employer!

Create 8-10 Stories Covering:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1. Success Story
   â€¢ Major project delivered
   â€¢ Positive impact
   â€¢ Technical excellence

2. Failure Story
   â€¢ Real failure
   â€¢ Lessons learned
   â€¢ How you improved

3. Leadership Example
   â€¢ Taking initiative
   â€¢ Guiding others
   â€¢ Positive outcome

   â€¢ Disagreement handled professionally
   â€¢ Communication skills
   â€¢ Win-win outcome

   â€¢ New technology/skill
   â€¢ How you learned
   â€¢ Applied successfully

   â€¢ Working with team
   â€¢ Your contribution
   â€¢ Team success

   â€¢ Complex challenge
   â€¢ Creative solution
   â€¢ Measurable result

   â€¢ Tight deadline
   â€¢ How you managed
   â€¢ Successful delivery

Make Stories Adaptable:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Example: API optimization story can be used for:
â€¢ Challenging project
â€¢ Problem-solving

Practice:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â–¡ Write down 8-10 stories

â–¡ Get feedback from friend

â•‘                   COMPANY-SPECIFIC VALUES                  â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Amazon - Leadership Principles (14 Principles)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Must know ALL 14 and prepare story for each!

Key Principles:
1. Customer Obsession
2. Ownership
3. Invent and Simplify
4. Learn and Be Curious
5. Hire and Develop the Best
6. Insist on the Highest Standards
7. Think Big
8. Bias for Action
9. Frugality
10. Earn Trust
11. Dive Deep
12. Have Backbone; Disagree and Commit
13. Deliver Results
14. Strive to be Earth's Best Employer (new)

Each question will test a specific principle!

Example:
"Tell me about a time you had to dive deep into a problem"

â€¢ "What does success look like in this role?"

â€¢ "How is the team structured?"
â€¢ "What's the collaboration style?"
â€¢ "How do you handle technical decisions?"

â€¢ "What are growth opportunities?"
â€¢ "How does the company support learning?"
â€¢ "What's the career progression?"

â€¢ "What are you most excited about for the company?"

â€¢ "What's the biggest challenge facing the team?"

âŒ Anything on the website (shows lack of research)
```

```bash
â–¡ No notes/cheatsheets
â–¡ Phone on silent

Mock Interview Structure (45 min):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Minutes 0-2: Introduction
â€¢ Interviewer introduces themselves
â€¢ Interviewee gives brief background
â€¢ Set the tone

Minutes 2-7: Problem Statement
â€¢ Interviewer explains problem
â€¢ Interviewee asks clarifying questions
â€¢ Discuss examples

Minutes 7-35: Coding
â€¢ Interviewee explains approach
â€¢ Writes code
â€¢ Tests solution
â€¢ Discusses complexity

Minutes 35-40: Follow-up Questions
â€¢ Optimization discussions
â€¢ Edge cases
â€¢ Alternative approaches

Minutes 40-45: Feedback
â€¢ Interviewer gives feedback
â€¢ Discuss what went well
â€¢ Areas to improve

After Interview:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â–¡ Take notes on feedback
â–¡ Identify specific improvements
â–¡ Practice weak areas
â–¡ Schedule next mock

Good Feedback Structure:
1. Positive (what they did well)
2. Areas to improve (specific)
3. Actionable suggestions

Example:
"You did a great job explaining your approach before coding
 and testing your solution thoroughly.

 One area to improve is communicating while writing code -
 there were a few minutes of silence.

 I'd suggest narrating your thought process as you code,
 like 'Now I'm iterating through the array to...'"
```

```bash
That's $50K+ over 5 years for a 30-minute conversation! ğŸ’°

Total Compensation Components:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1. Base Salary
â€¢ Fixed annual amount
â€¢ Guaranteed income
â€¢ Most important for budgeting

2. Signing Bonus
â€¢ One-time payment
â€¢ Often year 1 only
â€¢ Negotiable!
â€¢ May have clawback clause

3. Stock Options/RSUs (Equity)
â€¢ Ownership in company
â€¢ Vesting schedule (usually 4 years)
â€¢ RSUs: Restricted Stock Units (liquid companies)
â€¢ Options: Startup equity (illiquid)

4. Annual Bonus
â€¢ Performance-based
â€¢ Usually 10-20% of base
â€¢ Not guaranteed

5. Benefits
â€¢ Health insurance
â€¢ 401k matching
â€¢ PTO/vacation days
â€¢ Learning budget
â€¢ Remote work
â€¢ Relocation assistance

Total Comp Calculation:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Example FAANG Offer:

Base Salary: $150,000
Signing Bonus (Year 1): $50,000
Annual Bonus (Target 15%): $22,500
RSUs (4-year vest): $400,000 ($100K/year)

Year 1 Total: $150K + $50K + $22.5K + $100K = $322,500
Year 2-4 Total: $150K + $22.5K + $100K = $272,500/year

4-Year Total: $1,140,000
Average per year: $285,000

This is what you compare against other offers!

Phase 1: Initial Offer Received
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

DON'T:
âŒ Accept immediately (even if great!)
âŒ Give a number first
âŒ Show too much excitement

DO:
âœ… Thank them for the offer
âœ… Express genuine excitement about role
âœ… Ask for offer in writing
âœ… Request time to review (1-2 weeks standard)

Script:
"Thank you so much for the offer! I'm really excited about
 the opportunity and the team. Can you send me the written
 offer details? I'd like to review everything carefully
 and discuss with my family. When do you need a response by?"

Phase 2: Review Period (1-2 weeks)
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

What to Do:
â–¡ Get competing offers (if possible)
â–¡ Research market rates
â–¡ Calculate total comp
â–¡ Identify negotiation points
â–¡ Prepare your ask
â–¡ Practice negotiation conversation

Competing Offers:
Best leverage! Even if not accepting.
"I have another offer at $X, but I prefer your company"

Phase 3: Negotiation Call
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Opening (Start Positive):
"I'm very excited about this role and I think I'd be a
 great fit for the team. I've been reviewing the offer
 and did some market research..."

Present Your Case:
"Based on my research of market rates for this role/level
 in [location], and considering my [experience/skills/
 competing offers], I was hoping we could discuss the
 compensation."

Make Your Ask:
Be specific! Don't say "Can you do better?"

Good Ask:
"I was hoping for a base salary of $X, signing bonus of $Y,
 and equity of $Z. This would put me at a total comp of $W,
 which aligns with market rate for my experience level."

Justify Your Ask:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âœ… Market data (levels.fyi shows...)
âœ… Competing offers (I have offer at $X...)
âœ… Unique skills (My experience in Y is valuable...)
âœ… Cost of living (Relocating to expensive area...)
âœ… Leaving benefits (Walking away from $X in stock...)

Phase 4: Handling Responses
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

If They Say Yes:
"That works! Let me get this updated and send new offer."
â†’ Get it in writing, review, accept!

If They Say "That's above our range":
"I understand. What is possible within your range?
 Can we increase [signing bonus/equity/base]?"

If They Say "This is our best offer":
They're probably not! Try:
"I appreciate that. I'm really interested in joining,
 but the gap is significant. Is there any flexibility
 on [specific component]? Perhaps [creative solution]?"

Creative Solutions:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
If they can't move base salary:
â€¢ Higher signing bonus
â€¢ More equity
â€¢ Earlier review/promotion timeline
â€¢ Remote work flexibility
â€¢ Learning/conference budget
â€¢ Additional PTO
â€¢ Relocation assistance
â€¢ Performance bonus guarantee

If they can't move total comp:
â€¢ Earlier equity vesting
â€¢ Equity refresh guarantee
â€¢ Promotion timeline commitment
â€¢ Better title

Phase 5: Final Decision
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

When to Accept:
âœ… Comp is at market rate or above
âœ… You're excited about role/team
âœ… Good work-life balance
âœ… Growth opportunities
âœ… No major red flags

When to Walk Away:
âŒ Significantly below market (>20%)
âŒ Refused to negotiate at all
âŒ Red flags in process
âŒ Better offer elsewhere
âŒ Gut feeling says no

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   NEGOTIATION SCRIPTS                      â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Script 1: Initial Response
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"Thank you for the offer! I'm excited about the opportunity
 to join [Team/Company] and work on [specific project].

 I'd like some time to review the details carefully. Could
 you send me the written offer? When do you need my response?"

Script 2: Asking for More Time
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"I appreciate you sending the offer. I'm very interested,
 but I have [interviews/another offer] in progress. Would
 it be possible to extend the deadline by [X days]?"

Most companies will give you 1-2 weeks, some will extend to 4.

Script 3: Opening Negotiation
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"I'm very enthusiastic about this role. After reviewing
 the offer and researching market rates, I was hoping we
 could discuss the compensation package.

 Based on my [X years experience], [specific skills], and
 market data from [levels.fyi/Glassdoor], I was expecting
 a total compensation in the range of [X-Y].

 Is there room to adjust the offer?"

Script 4: With Competing Offer
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"I'm really excited about [Company] and the team. However,
 I do have a competing offer at [Other Company] with a
 total compensation of $X.

 [Company] is my top choice because of [specific reasons],
 but the compensation gap is significant. Is there
 flexibility to get closer to that range?"

Script 5: Asking for Specific Increase
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"I'm very interested in accepting the offer. However,
 I was hoping for:
 â€¢ Base salary of $X (currently offered $Y)
 â€¢ Signing bonus of $A (currently $B)
 â€¢ Equity of $C (currently $D)

 This would bring total comp to $Z, which aligns with
 market rate for this level. Is this possible?"

Script 6: If They Can't Meet Your Number
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"I understand there are budget constraints. I'm flexible
 on how we structure this. Could we:
 â€¢ Increase signing bonus instead of base?
 â€¢ Add more equity?
 â€¢ Commit to an earlier performance review?
 â€¢ Guarantee a promotion timeline?

 I really want to make this work."

Script 7: Accepting the Offer
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"Thank you for working with me on this! I'm excited to
 accept the offer and join the team. Looking forward to
 starting on [date]."

Script 8: Declining the Offer
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
"Thank you for the opportunity and for working with me
 through the negotiation. After careful consideration,
 I've decided to pursue another opportunity that's a
 better fit for me at this time.

 I really appreciated [specific positive], and I hope
 we can stay in touch for future opportunities."

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   NEGOTIATION DO'S AND DON'TS              â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

DO:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âœ… Always negotiate (expected!)
âœ… Be professional and polite
âœ… Do your research (market rates)
âœ… Get everything in writing
âœ… Ask for time to review
âœ… Consider total comp (not just base)
âœ… Have competing offers if possible
âœ… Be prepared to walk away
âœ… Negotiate in good faith
âœ… Express enthusiasm for role
âœ… Focus on value you bring
âœ… Be specific in your ask

DON'T:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ Accept first offer immediately
âŒ Give your current salary (if asked)
âŒ Make threats or ultimatums
âŒ Lie about competing offers
âŒ Negotiate just base (consider equity/bonus)
âŒ Be overly aggressive
âŒ Negotiate via email only (call better)
âŒ Forget to get offer in writing
âŒ Accept verbally before written offer
âŒ Negotiate if you won't accept

â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•—
â•‘                   SPECIAL SITUATIONS                       â•‘
â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

Situation 1: First Job Out of College
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Less leverage, but still negotiate!
â€¢ Focus on learning: "I'm excited to learn and grow.
  Based on my research, entry-level engineers at
  [Company] typically earn $X. Is there flexibility?"
â€¢ Even $5K matters early in career

Situation 2: Startup Equity
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Questions to Ask:
â–¡ How many shares outstanding?
â–¡ What % does my equity represent?
â–¡ Latest valuation?
â–¡ Vesting schedule?
â–¡ Cliff period?
â–¡ Preferred vs common stock?
â–¡ Exit scenarios?

Reality: Most startup equity = $0
Take if: You believe in company + base is acceptable

Situation 3: Internal Transfer/Promotion
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Still negotiate!
â€¢ Easier: "Market rate for [new level] is $X"
â€¢ Ask about: New equity grant, promotion bonus
â€¢ Timing: Try to align with review cycle

Situation 4: Counter-Offers from Current Employer
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Should you accept?

Usually NO because:
âŒ Why did it take leaving for raise?
âŒ Trust is broken
âŒ Statistics: 70% leave within 1 year anyway
âŒ New company knows you tried to leave

Accept only if:
âœ… You genuinely want to stay
âœ… They address root issues (not just money)
âœ… Relationship with manager is strong
âœ… Company is in good shape

Day 1: Receive Offer
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Recruiter calls: "We'd like to extend an offer!"
â€¢ You: "Thank you! I'm excited. Can you email details?
        When do you need a response?"
â€¢ Get offer in writing

Day 2-3: Research
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Check levels.fyi
â€¢ Calculate total comp
â€¢ Identify gaps
â€¢ Prepare your ask

Day 4-7: Negotiate
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Schedule call with recruiter
â€¢ Present your case
â€¢ Make specific ask
â€¢ Discuss back and forth

Day 8-10: Revised Offer
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Receive updated offer
â€¢ Review carefully
â€¢ Final negotiation if needed

Day 11-14: Decision
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Accept or decline
â€¢ Get final offer in writing
â€¢ Sign offer letter

Total: 2 weeks (standard timeline)
```

### Learn From Others' Failures ğŸš«

```bash

# INTERVIEW MISTAKES TO AVOID

Mistake 1: Starting Too Late
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I have interview next week, let me start LeetCode now"

Reality:
â€¢ Need 2-3 months minimum for serious prep
â€¢ Last-minute cramming doesn't work
â€¢ Pattern recognition takes time

Fix:
âœ… Start 3 months before applications
âœ… Consistent daily practice
âœ… Plan ahead

Mistake 2: Only Doing Easy Problems
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I'll just do Easy problems to build confidence"

Reality:
â€¢ Interviews have mostly Medium problems
â€¢ Easy doesn't prepare you for real interviews
â€¢ False sense of readiness

Fix:
âœ… Focus on Medium (70% of practice)
âœ… Easy for warm-up only
âœ… Some Hard for challenge

Mistake 3: Random Problem Solving
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I'll just solve whatever problem comes up"

Reality:
â€¢ No pattern recognition
â€¢ Inefficient learning
â€¢ Takes longer

Fix:
âœ… Follow structured plan (NeetCode 150, Blind 75)
âœ… Learn patterns
âœ… Solve by category

Mistake 4: Not Doing Mock Interviews
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I can solve problems, I'll be fine"

Reality:
â€¢ Interview pressure is different
â€¢ Communication is different
â€¢ First real interview is a shock

Fix:
âœ… 5+ mock interviews before real ones
âœ… Start 1 month before
âœ… Practice being watched

Mistake 5: Ignoring System Design
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I'm only mid-level, I don't need system design"

Reality:
â€¢ Many mid-level positions ask system design
â€¢ Senior interviews heavily weighted on it
â€¢ Takes time to learn

Fix:
âœ… Learn basics even if mid-level
âœ… 1 month prep minimum for senior+
âœ… Practice drawing diagrams

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I'll just wing the behavioral questions"

â€¢ 30-40% of interview decision
â€¢ Poor behavioral = rejection despite good technical
â€¢ Need prepared stories

Fix:
âœ… Prepare 8-10 STAR stories
âœ… Practice out loud
âœ… Research company values

Mistake 7: Jumping Straight to Code
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ [Gets problem] â†’ [Immediately starts coding]

Reality:
â€¢ Likely coding wrong solution
â€¢ Can't pivot once invested in code
â€¢ Shows poor planning

Fix:
âœ… Ask clarifying questions
âœ… Work through examples
âœ… Explain approach
âœ… Get approval
âœ… THEN code

Mistake 8: Coding in Silence
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ [Silent for 20 minutes while coding]

Reality:
â€¢ Interviewer can't follow your thinking
â€¢ Can't help if you're stuck
â€¢ Uncomfortable silence
â€¢ Looks like you're struggling

Fix:
âœ… Think out loud CONSTANTLY
âœ… Explain every decision
âœ… "Now I'm iterating through..."
âœ… Make it a conversation

Mistake 9: Not Testing Your Code
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "Looks good to me!" [without testing]

Reality:
â€¢ Code often has bugs
â€¢ Shows lack of thoroughness
â€¢ Interviewer will find bugs

Fix:
âœ… Always test with examples
âœ… Walk through line by line
âœ… Check edge cases
âœ… Find your own bugs

Mistake 10: Giving Up Too Easily
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I don't know" [sits in silence]

Reality:
â€¢ Interview is about process, not just answer
â€¢ Interviewer wants to see you try
â€¢ Giving up = automatic fail

Fix:
âœ… Try brute force first
âœ… Talk through what you're thinking
âœ… Ask for hints if really stuck
âœ… Never give up!

Mistake 11: Not Asking Clarifying Questions
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ [Hears problem] â†’ "Got it, let me code"

â€¢ Missing important constraints
â€¢ Solving wrong problem
â€¢ Shows carelessness

Fix:
âœ… Always ask 5-10 questions
âœ… Verify understanding
âœ… Discuss edge cases
âœ… Confirm output format

Mistake 12: Ignoring Hints
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ Interviewer: "Have you considered using a hash table?"
   You: "No, I think this approach is better..."

â€¢ Hints are there to help you!
â€¢ Ignoring shows stubbornness
â€¢ Interviewer knows the optimal solution

Fix:
âœ… Always explore interviewer's suggestions
âœ… "That's a great idea, let me think about that"
âœ… Be coachable

Mistake 13: Not Explaining Complexity
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ [Finishes code] â†’ "Done!"

â€¢ Interviewers expect complexity analysis
â€¢ Shows understanding of efficiency
â€¢ Required for strong performance

Fix:
âœ… Always state time and space complexity
âœ… Explain why
âœ… Discuss trade-offs

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

â€¢ Code quality matters
â€¢ Shows professionalism
â€¢ Hard to follow for interviewer

Fix:
âœ… Meaningful variable names
âœ… Clean formatting
âœ… Logical structure
âœ… Comments for complex parts

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

â€¢ Ego is a red flag

âœ… Be humble
âœ… Work together

âŒ "My boss was terrible, the company was a mess..."

â€¢ Major red flag
â€¢ Shows unprofessionalism
â€¢ They wonder if you'll say this about them

âœ… Stay positive
âœ… "I learned a lot, now seeking new challenges"
âœ… Focus on growth, not complaints

â€¢ Sounds arrogant

â€¢ Shows poor teamwork

âœ… Use "I" for your contributions
âœ… Acknowledge team
âœ… Be specific about YOUR role

â€¢ Everyone says this

â€¢ Shows lack of interest

âŒ "I'm not good enough for FAANG"

â€¢ You miss 100% of shots you don't take

âœ… Worst case: Practice
âœ… Best case: Dream job!

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

â€¢ Focus on YOUR improvement

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
âŒ "I'll code 12 hours/day until interview"

â€¢ Unsustainable

â€¢ Mental exhaustion in actual interview

âœ… 2-3 hours/day is enough
âœ… Take rest days
âœ… Marathon, not sprint
âœ… Sleep well before interviews
```

```bash
Sample Thank You:
"Hi [Name],

Thank you for taking the time to speak with me today about
the [Position] role. I really enjoyed our discussion about
[specific topic] and learning more about [team/project].

I'm even more excited about the opportunity to contribute
to [something specific], and I believe my experience with
[relevant skill] would be valuable to the team.

Looking forward to hearing from you!

Best regards,

Scenario 1: Internet Dies
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Action Plan:
1. Have recruiter's phone number ready
2. Call immediately to explain
3. Use phone hotspot as backup
4. Ask to reschedule if necessary

Scenario 2: Computer Crashes
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Action Plan:
1. Have backup device ready
2. Join from phone/tablet
3. Explain situation calmly
4. Continue interview or reschedule

Scenario 3: You're Running Late
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Action Plan:
1. Email/call recruiter ASAP
2. Give realistic ETA
3. Apologize sincerely
4. Join as soon as possible

Scenario 4: You Freeze/Blank Out
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Action Plan:
1. Take deep breath
2. "Let me think for a moment..."
3. Write down what you know
4. Ask clarifying question to restart thinking
5. Start with brute force approach

Scenario 5: You Realize You Made a Mistake
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Action Plan:
1. Acknowledge it: "Wait, I see an issue..."
2. Explain the problem
3. Fix it
4. Test again
5. Don't panic - shows debugging skills!
```
